Following the surrender ceremony, Mothma gave Sinjir a bottle of expensive [lachrymead](/wiki/Lachrymead "Lachrymead") [wine](/wiki/Wine "Wine") to thank him for his services to the New Republic.[[109]](#cite_note-Empire's_End-109)

The Galactic Concordance formally ended hostilities between the New Republic and the defeated Galactic Empire.[[110]](#cite_note-TFA_VD-110) The treaty forced the Empire to remain inside predetermined territories within the [Core Worlds](/wiki/Core_Worlds "Core Worlds") and the Inner Rim. Mothma urged the Republic to remain vigilant in the event that the conflict returned, and temporarily kept the New Republic Starfleet on wartime funding and alert status.[[98]](#cite_note-Lost_Stars-98) Once it became clear that the war was over, the Galactic Senate fulfilled Mothma's goal and passed the [Military Disarmament Act](/wiki/Military_Disarmament_Act "Military Disarmament Act"). However, the remnants of the Empire disappeared into the [Unknown Regions](/wiki/Unknown_Regions "Unknown Regions").[[110]](#cite_note-TFA_VD-110) Some time during her tenure, Mothma further reformed the Senate by establishing that member worlds would act as the Senate's capital on a rotating basis.[[111]](#cite_note-Hosnian_Prime_Databank-111) Rotating the capital, and in particular keeping it off of Coruscant, did much to convince member worlds that the New Republic would be different from its predecessor governments.[[110]](#cite_note-TFA_VD-110)

#### Meetings with Syndulla[]

:   "*We have to prepare for the worst and hope for the best.*"
:   ―Hera Syndulla, to Mon Mothma[[112]](#cite_note-Part_Seven-112)

 [![Chancellor Mothma with members of the New Republic Senate](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/98/TheSenateSquad.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20230407145234) [![Chancellor Mothma with members of the New Republic Senate](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/98/TheSenateSquad.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20230407145234)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/98/TheSenateSquad.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20230407145234) 

Chancellor Mothma with members of the New Republic Senate

 

In [9 ABY](/wiki/9_ABY "9 ABY"),[[113]](#cite_note-Date-113) during which time Coruscant was serving as capital of the New Republic[[114]](#cite_note-Insider_228-114) after Chandrila had taken the flag for a time,[[115]](#cite_note-Chapter_12:_The_Siege-115) Chancellor Mothma and four members of the New Republic Senate, including [Hamato Xiono](/wiki/Hamato_Xiono "Hamato Xiono"), held a meeting over hologram with General Syndulla.[[19]](#cite_note-Part_Three-19) Syndulla, who had just been attacked by Imperial loyalists at [Santhe Shipyards](/wiki/Santhe_Shipyards "Santhe Shipyards") on [Corellia](/wiki/Corellia "Corellia") while investigating the work of[[116]](#cite_note-Part_Two-116) the recently-[escaped](/wiki/Attack_on_the_Vesper "Attack on the Vesper")[[117]](#cite_note-Part_One-117) Imperial industrialist [Morgan Elsbeth](/wiki/Morgan_Elsbeth "Morgan Elsbeth"),[[116]](#cite_note-Part_Two-116) proclaimed that the New Republic had to prepare for the worst and expressed concern over the potential return of Grand Admiral Thrawn, a project that the loyalists at the shipyard had been contributing to.[[19]](#cite_note-Part_Three-19)

### Retirement[]

Sometime later, Mothma became ill and stepped down as Chancellor. However, her successors lacked Mothma's charisma, and failed to create that same political consensus as she did. In her absence, the New Republic fell into chaos and the Galactic Senate became divided into two factions: the [Populists](/wiki/Populists "Populists"), who believed that individual member planets should retain their full sovereignty, and the [Centrists](/wiki/Centrists "Centrists"), who favored a stronger galactic government and a larger military by [28 ABY](/wiki/28_ABY "28 ABY"). Mothma showed her personal support for Organa after it was publicly revealed that she was the daughter of Darth Vader. Her message to Organa indicated that she had suspected the truth for some time before the announcement.[[118]](#cite_note-Bloodline-118)

### Legacy[]

:   "*The likes of Mon Mothma are, of course, legendary for their leadership of the Rebel Alliance and then the New Republic. There is a reason why her life and career are considered key parts of school education.*"
:   ―Beaumont Kin, *The Rise and Fall of the Galactic Empire*[[60]](#cite_note-RiseFall-60)

In several ways, Mon Mothma's actions contributed to the New Republic's eventual undoing. Her drive for ensuring peace and demilitarization eventually left the New Republic in a weakened state of unpreparedness that lacked the strength to combat the rise of the First Order.[[119]](#cite_note-TSWB-119) The New Republic she quickly built fractured without her strong presence, and in no small part was caused by the influence of the draconian [First Order](/wiki/First_Order "First Order")'s growing strength that was not revealed for [decades](/wiki/Standard_decade "Standard decade").[[28]](#cite_note-HC_40-28) Nevertheless, decentralized defense forces, [fringers](/wiki/Fringer "Fringer") who had taken for granted the New Republic's limited enforcement of interstellar law, and ordinary citizens of the galaxy alike united against the oppression of the First Order. They formed a [Citizens' Fleet](/wiki/Citizens%27_Fleet "Citizens' Fleet") that joined the Resistance at the [Battle of Exegol](/wiki/Battle_of_Exegol "Battle of Exegol"), finally liberating the galaxy from the Sith and inspiring a galaxy-wide [uprising against the First Order](/wiki/Uprising_against_the_First_Order "Uprising against the First Order").[[120]](#cite_note-TROS_VD-120)

Due to her importance to the rise of the rebellion and era of the New Republic, Mothma was mentioned throughout *[The Rise and Fall of the Galactic Empire](/wiki/The_Rise_and_Fall_of_the_Galactic_Empire "The Rise and Fall of the Galactic Empire")*, a historical text published by the [historian](/wiki/Historian "Historian") and [Resistance trooper](/wiki/Resistance_trooper "Resistance trooper") [Beaumont Kin](/wiki/Beaumont_Kin "Beaumont Kin") in the hopes of leading the galaxy away from Imperial ideology once and for all. In the text, Kin reflected on Mothma's governmental decisions after the Galactic Civil War and wrote that the outcome of those choices could not be discussed without also touching on the rationale for each decision. Kin pondered in the text if Mothma had been scarred by the recent conflict, while also musing he may himself be scarred by war. He found he could not bring himself to overly critique Mothma's choices, reflecting that she had wanted to believe the bloodshed was worth its outcome and making note of all the limits that had existed on the establishment of her new government.[[60]](#cite_note-RiseFall-60)

## Personality and traits[]

:   "*War is not a state of being. It is meant to be a temporary chaos between periods of peace. Some want it to be the course of things: a default fact of existence. But I will not let that be so.*"
:   ―Mon Mothma, shortly after the death of Emperor Palpatine[[18]](#cite_note-Aftermath-18)

 [![Mon Mothma, during her time as a member of the Galactic Senate, wore an elegant robe of , a  mantle, and a , and sported a simple Chandrilan hairstyle](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/d9/MonMothma2.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20070615223341) [![Mon Mothma, during her time as a member of the Galactic Senate, wore an elegant robe of , a  mantle, and a , and sported a simple Chandrilan hairstyle](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/d9/MonMothma2.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20070615223341)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/d9/MonMothma2.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20070615223341) 

Mon Mothma, during her time as a member of the Galactic Senate, wore an elegant robe of [fleuréline weave](/wiki/Fleur%C3%A9line_weave "Fleuréline weave"), a [shraa silk](/wiki/Shraa_silk "Shraa silk") mantle, and a [hanna pendant](/wiki/Hanna_pendant "Hanna pendant"), and sported a simple Chandrilan hairstyle.[[3]](#cite_note-Character_Encyclopedia-3)

 

Mon Mothma was a [human](/wiki/Human "Human") [female](/wiki/Gender "Gender") with [auburn](/wiki/Color "Color") [hair](/wiki/Hair "Hair"), pale blue-green [eyes](/wiki/Eye "Eye"), and light skin.[[5]](#cite_note-RotJ_paperback_novel-5) Her opposition to authoritarianism that led Mothma to help form the Rebel Alliance. She pursued peace during the Clone Wars, but she was willing to fight to restore democracy to the galaxy.[[32]](#cite_note-Mon_Mothma_Bio_Gallery-32) Her ideals led her to become the first chancellor of the New Republic, where she pushed to avoid the mistakes that the Galactic Republic had made during the Clone Wars. Though strong executive powers were granted to her, she wanted nothing of the sort and believed them to be destructive to the democratic process.[[18]](#cite_note-Aftermath-18) During her time as a Republic senator, Mothma held pacifist beliefs which occasionally led to conflict with Amidala,[[13]](#cite_note-Queen's_Shadow-13) though the two never truly fought and they remained close allies.[[29]](#cite_note-Queen's_Hope-29) In fact, Amidala was able to mend the divide between Mothma and Bail Organa, helping the two friends to work better together. After detonating the assassin Soujen Vak-Nhalis's self-destruction mechanism to prevent his attack on the Imperial capital, Mothma was caught in the blast and, after surgery, lost her stomach, instead receiving a cybernetic replacement that took training to use. Her heart had also been hit by debris and retained microscopic pieces of metal. However, knowing that her body was not entirely her own felt true, as such was how she felt after her interrogation during the earliest days of the Empire.[[7]](#cite_note-MOF-7)

Mothma recongized that her instincts for purity, pacifism, and justice were tainted in the wake of Soujen's death and the failure of the Imperial Rebirth Act; while at the time she had told herself she could not justify murder as a political weapon, only to kill Soujen to prevent such from happening, she was left with the memory that she had ended his life and then found herself trending down the path of rebellion to unseat Palpatine anyway.[[7]](#cite_note-MOF-7) Mothma was a courageous and outspoken Senator in the Imperial Senate who criticized the Empire's increasingly authoritarian and repressive policies. The final straw that broke the [bantha](/wiki/Bantha "Bantha")'s back came when Mothma denounced the Emperor in a live [HoloNet](/wiki/HoloNet "HoloNet") speech for his role in the Ghorman Massacre. Despite becoming a fugitive, Mothma refused to hide herself but was determined to take dangerous risks in order to fulfill her goal of creating the Rebel Alliance. As a leader, Mothma preferred to lead by example in order to gain the respect of her underlings. Mothma also took the time to build friendships with other rebel fighters, like Hera Syndulla and Garazeb Orrelios.[[69]](#cite_note-Secret_Cargo-69) After the Imperial Senate was dissolved and Bail Organa was killed on Alderaan, Mothma invested herself fully into the Rebellion. As its leader, she made difficult decisions, a number of which would continue to haunt her. Despite this, she remained strong due to the individuals she worked with in Alliance High Command.[[121]](#cite_note-HC_20-121)

Mothma's devotion to her ideals did prove difficult at times. After the Empire's massacre on Kashyyyk, she thought diplomacy was dead and considered becoming a fighter pilot in the war against the Empire, but she learned that she provided more value to the Rebellion as its leader than as a soldier.[[102]](#cite_note-Beware_the_Power-102) When she learned of the existence of the second Death Star, she immediately believed that they could defeat it and resolved to get to work.[[101]](#cite_note-SW_2020_28-101) Later, when she learned that the Emperor intended to destroy Chandrila with the Death Star II as a means of silencing her, Mon Mothma struggled with the fear that her actions would endanger her people. However, she refused to allow herself to be ruled by fear and regarded giving into her fear as tantamount to surrendering to the Empire.[[20]](#cite_note-Moving_Target-20) Mothma viewed many of the simplistic Chandrilan customs favored by her daughter Leida as being outdated in modern times.[[58]](#cite_note-Leida_Databank-58) Mothma's arranged marriage to Perrin was an unhappy one, which made the sight of her daughter going down a similar path upsetting to her.[[55]](#cite_note-Space_Moms-55) Mothma saw Leia Organa in a way akin to a younger sister, almost as a daughter.[[66]](#cite_note-The_Princess_and_the_Scoundrel-66)

 [![Mon Mothma in the later years of the Galactic Civil War](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/5f/MonMothmaspeaks-ROTJ.png/revision/latest?cb=20250911134514) [![Mon Mothma in the later years of the Galactic Civil War](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/5f/MonMothmaspeaks-ROTJ.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/300?cb=20250911134514)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/5f/MonMothmaspeaks-ROTJ.png/revision/latest?cb=20250911134514) 

Mon Mothma in the later years of the Galactic Civil War

 

Despite her position as Chancellor of the New Republic, Mothma was wary of abusing her powers due to Palpatine's legacy. She was prepared to reduce the powers of her own office and the New Republic military once the threat of the Empire had been ended.[[18]](#cite_note-Aftermath-18) As the head of government, Mothma developed a sense of pragmatism since she had to manage a state that was also embroiled in a galactic war. Mothma was aware of the strains on the New Republic's resources and was reluctant to deploy military forces to Kashyyyk. Mothma's pragmatism contrasted with the idealism of Princess Leia, who was unwilling to let obstacles block her goal to liberate the Wookiee species. Believing that the Empire was facing defeat, Mothma agreed to peace talks with Rae Sloane. As a politician, Mothma sought to capitalize on the liberation of the Ashmead's Lock prisoners as an opportunity to win more worlds to the New Republic.[[107]](#cite_note-Life_Debt-107)

As Chancellor, Mon Mothma was skillful and savvy but strove to keep in touch with her constituents. Despite her powers and privileges, Mothma saw herself as serving the galaxy. She consciously struggled not to become an autocratic dictator like the late Palpatine. Mothma walked a fine balance between keeping the New Republic strong without turning it into a force for oppression. While Chancellor Mothma was sympathetic to the plight of Temmin and Sinjir who had loved ones and friends on Jakku, she was still determined to abide by the rules and norms of the New Republic. As a politician, Mothma preferred to use the system to achieve her goals.[[109]](#cite_note-Empire's_End-109)

Despite facing low popular ratings (39%) and having to contend with the hawkish Senator Tolwar Wartol, Mothma resolved to continue leading the New Republic. Mothma used her friendly connections and political savvy to outwit Wartol's plot to discredit her leadership. Chancellor Mothma was also a good talent spotter. She recruited the former Imperial loyalty officer Sinjir as one of her new advisers. She admired Sinjir's ingenious plan to convince five dissident senators to change their votes in favor of her resolution to intervene on Jakku. Though Mothma grieved the death of her friend Auxi during Senator Wartol's failed assassination attempt on her life, she remained resolute and led the New Republic's peace negotiations with Grand Vizier Mas Amedda. While presiding over the Empire's surrender, Mothma took care to co-opt non-combatant Imperial functionaries in order to ensure a smooth political transition.[[109]](#cite_note-Empire's_End-109)

## Skills and abilities[]

In addition to being a keen diplomat, Mon Mothma trained as a fighter pilot, although she never actually saw battle.[[102]](#cite_note-Beware_the_Power-102) Mon Mothma was also a skilled speaker who appealed to her listener's hopes, dreams, and values. While Mothma was a politician, she also knew how to detach two docked starships.[[69]](#cite_note-Secret_Cargo-69) As a politician, Chancellor Mothma was able to switch from formal talk to plain speaking based on the situation. Despite being wounded in her left arm, Mothma insisted on keeping her arm and took exercises to strengthen it.[[109]](#cite_note-Empire's_End-109)

## Equipment[]

Mothma wore a white Chandrilan [tunic](/wiki/Clothing "Clothing") and mantle while serving in the Republic Senate.[[122]](#cite_note-VE-122)

## Behind the scenes[]

### Development and portrayal[]

:   "*Certainly people are always very envious of me. When I join a new theater company, the other actors look down the program, see my* Return of the Jedi *credit and say, 'Oh, you were part of* Star Wars*.' I smile and say, 'Yes, but only for twenty-six and a half seconds.'*"
:   ―Caroline Blakiston[[123]](#cite_note-Galaxy_Magazine_12-123)

 [![Since her brief appearance in Return of the Jedi, Mon Mothma has become a vital figure in Star Wars storytelling.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/6/6e/Manybothansdied.png/revision/latest?cb=20130404024024) [![Since her brief appearance in Return of the Jedi, Mon Mothma has become a vital figure in Star Wars storytelling.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/6/6e/Manybothansdied.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/300?cb=20130404024024)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/6/6e/Manybothansdied.png/revision/latest?cb=20130404024024) 

Since her brief appearance in *Return of the Jedi*, Mon Mothma has become a vital figure in *Star Wars* storytelling.

 

Mon Mothma was first introduced in the [1983](/wiki/1983 "1983") film [*Star Wars*: Episode VI *Return of the Jedi*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_VI_Return_of_the_Jedi "Star Wars: Episode VI Return of the Jedi"), directed by [Richard Marquand](/wiki/Richard_Marquand "Richard Marquand") from a script by [George Lucas](/wiki/George_Lucas "George Lucas") and [Lawrence Kasdan](/wiki/Lawrence_Kasdan "Lawrence Kasdan"). She was portrayed by [Caroline Blakiston](/wiki/Caroline_Blakiston "Caroline Blakiston"),[[6]](#cite_note-Episode_VI-6) who was cast while working in [Manchester](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manchester "wikipedia:Manchester"), [England](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/England "wikipedia:England") on a television series. Blakiston met with costume designers in a Manchester hotel room to fit her for a costume and discuss what kind of hairstyle her character would sport, but it was ultimately decided she would use her own red hair.[[124]](#cite_note-Blakiston_interview-124) Blakiston was provided with an initial script for her brief part in the film, but, upon arriving on set, she learned that her lines had been changed and she would have to learn an entirely new monologue. This proved somewhat stressful, particularly as a result of the dialogue containing *[Star Wars](/wiki/Star_Wars "Star Wars")* terminology like the word "Bothan."[[124]](#cite_note-Blakiston_interview-124)[[125]](#cite_note-Knightley-125) While in production, Blakiston came up with her own idea for the character's backstory, hoping to find inspiration in the *Star Wars* [saga's](/wiki/Star_Wars_saga "Star Wars saga") classical underpinnings. She felt that the name "Mon Mothma" bore a similarity to the words "Moon Mother," and as a result she saw her character as someone who would be cool and collected.[[125]](#cite_note-Knightley-125) Blakiston had to re-record her dialogue after it was discovered that pigeons roosting in the set were audible in the original recordings.[[126]](#cite_note-Old_Databank-126)

A younger version of Mon Mothma appeared in the [2005](/wiki/2005 "2005") film [*Star Wars*: Episode III *Revenge of the Sith*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_III_Revenge_of_the_Sith "Star Wars: Episode III Revenge of the Sith"), written and directed by George Lucas. [Genevieve O'Reilly](/wiki/Genevieve_O%27Reilly "Genevieve O'Reilly") was chosen to portray the role due to her resemblance to Blakiston,[[126]](#cite_note-Old_Databank-126) and she filmed a few scenes for the film that were meant to set up the eventual formation of the Rebel Alliance.[[127]](#cite_note-DVD-127) Before filming, O'Reilly studied Blakiston's performance, hoping to capture the character's voice and mannerisms.[[126]](#cite_note-Old_Databank-126) The scenes in which O'Reilly had a speaking role were cut and later included on the film's [DVD release](/wiki/Star_Wars_home_video_releases#Star_Wars_Episode_III:_Revenge_of_the_Sith "Star Wars home video releases")[[127]](#cite_note-DVD-127) though O'Reilly did appear in one scene in the final film in a non-speaking role.[[12]](#cite_note-Episode_III-12) Blakiston hoped to have a part in the film, asking Lucas if she could appear as her character's grandmother, but she never received a response from the director.[[124]](#cite_note-Blakiston_interview-124)

The character later appeared in an expanded role in the animated television series *[Star Wars: The Clone Wars](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars "Star Wars: The Clone Wars")*. In the three episodes in which the character had a speaking role, she was voiced by actress [Kath Soucie](/wiki/Kath_Soucie "Kath Soucie").[[38]](#cite_note-Senate_Murders-38)[[39]](#cite_note-Heroes_on_Both_Sides-39)[[40]](#cite_note-Pursuit_of_Peace-40) Her role as leader of the Rebel Alliance and New Republic has also been expanded upon in several [canonical](/wiki/Canon "Canon") *Star Wars* tales.[[84]](#cite_note-Star_Wars_4-84)[[20]](#cite_note-Moving_Target-20)[[18]](#cite_note-Aftermath-18) O'Reilly would voice Mothma in the *[Star Wars Rebels](/wiki/Star_Wars_Rebels "Star Wars Rebels")* animated television series.[[69]](#cite_note-Secret_Cargo-69) Mothma has also proven to be a consistent character in the works of author [Alexander Freed](/wiki/Alexander_Freed "Alexander Freed"), who has described her as a character who makes every story better.[[128]](#cite_note-Freed_Mothma-128)

### *Rogue One: A Star Wars Story*[]

:   "*Rogue One was a really exciting piece to be a part of. It felt like a genuinely creative project. My memories of it were that it was shot almost like an indie film at times. It was very exciting, and it felt like a hotbed of creativity.*"
:   ―Genevieve O'Reilly[[129]](#cite_note-ProductionBrief-129)

O'Reilly returned to the role for the film *[Rogue One: A Star Wars Story](/wiki/Rogue_One:_A_Star_Wars_Story "Rogue One: A Star Wars Story")*.[[130]](#cite_note-EW_Rogue_One-130) According to [Alexander Freed](/wiki/Alexander_Freed "Alexander Freed"), the author of the [*Rogue One: A Star Wars Story* novelization](/wiki/Rogue_One:_A_Star_Wars_Story_(novelization) "Rogue One: A Star Wars Story (novelization)"), he would have loved to write more about Mon Mothma in the novel. He later had the opportunity to do so in the story "[Contingency Plan](/wiki/Contingency_Plan "Contingency Plan")" of the [2017](/wiki/2017 "2017") anthology *[From a Certain Point of View](/wiki/From_a_Certain_Point_of_View "From a Certain Point of View")*.[[131]](#cite_note-Twitter-131)

### *Andor* television series[]

:   "*She's very enigmatic in all the previous incarnations. People don't have any idea how complicated and difficult Mon Mothma's life has been — her character in many ways has the hardest road of our whole show, what she goes through and the pressure on her. She's this woman who's trapped in a box with everybody watching her, and she has this incredibly potent secret life where she's put herself at great risk by supporting the rebellion. There's no freedom from anxiety in this woman's life, and yet she has to not only endure, but she also has to thrive.*"
:   ―Tony Gilroy[[129]](#cite_note-ProductionBrief-129)

O'Reilly reprised her role as Mothma in the *[Star Wars: Andor](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Andor "Star Wars: Andor")* television series.[[53]](#cite_note-Aldhani-53) Writer and executive producer [Tony Gilroy](/wiki/Tony_Gilroy "Tony Gilroy") was interested in exploring the mystique surrounding Mothma and presenting her in a surprising light.[[129]](#cite_note-ProductionBrief-129) He also wanted to explore the orthodoxy and constructs Mothma would have to live with due to becoming a senator and getting married at the age of 16.[[132]](#cite_note-Marriage-132) Gilroy called her the "figurehead of liberal democracy that will fail"[[133]](#cite_note-Mothma-133) and compared her to [US House Speaker](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speaker_of_the_United_States_House_of_Representatives "wikipedia:Speaker of the United States House of Representatives") [Nancy Pelosi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nancy_Pelosi "wikipedia:Nancy Pelosi").[[134]](#cite_note-Pelosi-134) [Chuck Wendig](/wiki/Chuck_Wendig "Chuck Wendig"), author of the 2015–2017 [*The Aftermath Trilogy*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Aftermath_Trilogy "Star Wars: The Aftermath Trilogy"), had previously described her as a "fairly centrist leader" who proved the difficulty of good governance.[[135]](#cite_note-Wendig_Empire's_End-135) Gilroy realized that there was not much canon information on Mothma, allowing him to make Vel Sartha her cousin.[[136]](#cite_note-Easter_eggs-136) He wanted Mothma and the other legacy characters to not provide fan service.[[137]](#cite_note-Real_People-137) Executive producer [Sanne Wohlenberg](/wiki/Sanne_Wohlenberg "Sanne Wohlenberg") and her team put much thought into how they would represent Mothma and show her journey, and they stayed aware of where she ended up in *Rogue One*.[[129]](#cite_note-ProductionBrief-129)

 [![Mon Mothma's costume was designed by Michael Wilkinson.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/3/33/MonMothmaCostumeSDCC.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20230219034435) [![Mon Mothma's costume was designed by Michael Wilkinson.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/3/33/MonMothmaCostumeSDCC.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/260?cb=20230219034435)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/3/33/MonMothmaCostumeSDCC.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20230219034435) 

Mon Mothma's costume was designed by Michael Wilkinson.

 

Production designer [Luke Hull](/wiki/Luke_Hull "Luke Hull") created a sketch of Mon Mothma exiting a Senate limousine on Coruscant.[[138]](#cite_note-Period_drama-138) Costume designer [Michael Wilkinson](/wiki/Michael_Wilkinson "Michael Wilkinson") styled Mothma in flowing robes that evoked her sense of style seen in her *Revenge of the Sith* deleted scene. He knew that Mothma was a senator from Chandrila who was stationed on Coruscant, so he thought about people from different countries that work at the [United Nations building](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Headquarters_of_the_United_Nations "wikipedia:Headquarters of the United Nations") in [New York](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York "wikipedia:New York"). Wilkinson's team intended to bring elements of clothing from Mothma's home, so they came up with a set of colors and textures mainly drawn from other iterations of her. He leaned into pale neutral tones, and Mothma was given slightly shimmery organic textures with hints of metals.[[139]](#cite_note-Dressing_the_galaxy-139)

The crew tried to show Mothma's public face and the private woman within it.[[140]](#cite_note-Never_thought-140) O'Reilly was delighted to have an opportunity to better understand her character.[[129]](#cite_note-ProductionBrief-129) She also wanted to explore Mothma as a Rebel leader and as a woman,[[140]](#cite_note-Never_thought-140) which included showing the private face of someone who navigates through systems of oppression.[[141]](#cite_note-Potent_Moment-141) O'Reilly tried to understand the pain and personal cost felt by Caroline Blakiston in *Return of the Jedi*, and she enjoyed learning more about Mothma's life.[[140]](#cite_note-Never_thought-140) She was excited for the audience to see Mothma's journey of becoming the Rebel leader that she is in *Rogue One*.[[141]](#cite_note-Potent_Moment-141) O'Reilly wanted her character's new look in the show to reflect her new stage as a successful member of high society.[[132]](#cite_note-Marriage-132) Scenes in the Chandrilan embassy were filmed in a practically built set that had a wraparound [LED](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Light-emitting_diode "wikipedia:Light-emitting diode") screen that used [StageCraft](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/StageCraft "wikipedia:StageCraft") technology.[[142]](#cite_note-Slashfilm-142)

Composer [Nicholas Britell](/wiki/Nicholas_Britell "Nicholas Britell") created a musical signature for Mothma.[[143]](#cite_note-Rustling_leaves-143) For [Season Two](/wiki/Andor_Season_2 "Andor Season 2"), Michael Wilkinson worked on costumes that would evolve Mothma into the leader of the Rebellion.[[139]](#cite_note-Dressing_the_galaxy-139) In an interview with *Tech Radar*, O'Reilly and [Faye Marsay](/wiki/Faye_Marsay "Faye Marsay")—who played Mothma's cousin [Vel Sartha](/wiki/Vel_Sartha "Vel Sartha") in the series—reflected on their characters, with Marsay saying that, to Sartha, their relationship was not difficult and instead was one of tough circumstances: while Sartha acted on the frontlines of rebellion, Mothma was more in the shadows.[[144]](#cite_note-Many_cards-144) Factoring in Mothma's mother in regards to Leida's wedding, O'Reilly mentioned how "within the dialogue" there were "three generations of women," which turned the scene into a very "interconnected, intergenerational story." Further, she had pushed Gilroy to give Mothma a scene in which she gave Leida an out of the wedding, which culminated in the scene where Mothma does, but Leida gives what O'Reilly reflected to be a "pretty brutal" response.[[145]](#cite_note-YahooNews-145) After the conclusion of *Andor*, O'Reilly reflected on the wonderful surprise that returning to *Star Wars* had been and how *Andor* revealed more about Mothma to her. While she was unsure if it was possible to push Mothma's character further, she was open to the idea of returning once again.[[146]](#cite_note-Goldderby-146)

### Discrepancies[]

:   "*Bail Organa of Alderaan. How long have you known him?*"  
    "*Since I first joined the Senate, I suppose.*"  
    "*And how long ago was that?*"  
    "*You know the answer.*"  
    "*How long ago, please?*"  
    "*Thirteen years? Just about.*"
:   ―Mon Mothma, under Imperial interrogation[[7]](#cite_note-MOF-7)

According to *[Star Wars: The Rebel Files](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Rebel_Files "Star Wars: The Rebel Files")*, Mothma was elected senator in "[8 BFE](/wiki/Imperial_calendar "Imperial calendar")," i.e. 8 [years](/wiki/Standard_year "Standard year") before the [proclamation](/wiki/Proclamation_of_the_New_Order "Proclamation of the New Order") of the [Galactic Empire](/wiki/Galactic_Empire "Galactic Empire")[[22]](#cite_note-Rebel_Files-22) in [19 BBY](/wiki/19_BBY "19 BBY"),[[147]](#cite_note-Galactic_Atlas-147) which would place her election in [27 BBY](/wiki/27_BBY "27 BBY").[[22]](#cite_note-Rebel_Files-22)[[147]](#cite_note-Galactic_Atlas-147) However, in the novel *[Queen's Shadow](/wiki/Queen%27s_Shadow "Queen's Shadow")*, Mon Mothma says that she was "very new to the Senate when [Padmé Amidala] made [her] speech as Queen of Naboo,"[[13]](#cite_note-Queen's_Shadow-13) referring to a scene of the movie [*Star Wars*: Episode I *The Phantom Menace*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_I_The_Phantom_Menace "Star Wars: Episode I The Phantom Menace").[[148]](#cite_note-Episode_I-148) According to *[Star Wars: Galactic Atlas](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Galactic_Atlas "Star Wars: Galactic Atlas")*, the events of the movie took place in [32 BBY](/wiki/32_BBY "32 BBY"),[[147]](#cite_note-Galactic_Atlas-147) which would place Mothma's election that year or earlier.[[13]](#cite_note-Queen's_Shadow-13)[[147]](#cite_note-Galactic_Atlas-147) In *[Reign of the Empire: The Mask of Fear](/wiki/Reign_of_the_Empire:_The_Mask_of_Fear "Reign of the Empire: The Mask of Fear")*, the novel's events taking place in 19 BBY, Mothma stated that she joined the Senate nearly thirteen years ago, also placing her election circa 32 BBY.[[7]](#cite_note-MOF-7)

In the novel *[Leia, Princess of Alderaan](/wiki/Leia,_Princess_of_Alderaan "Leia, Princess of Alderaan")*, both Mothma and Winmey Lenz are identified as the Senior Senator of Chandrila.[[64]](#cite_note-Leia_Princess_of_Alderaan-64) "[Welcome to the Rebellion](/wiki/Welcome_to_the_Rebellion "Welcome to the Rebellion")" went onto corroborate that it was Mothma who served as Senior Senator.[[21]](#cite_note-Welcome_to_the_Rebellion-21) As such, this article assumes Mothma acted as Senior Senator, not Lenz.

### Role in *Star Wars* Legends[]

:   "*This great struggle is a people's struggle: a struggle between the strong and the weak, the rich and the poor, the cruel and the gentle.*"
:   ―Mon Mothma, describing the Rebellion in a quote from the *[The Rebel Alliance Sourcebook](/wiki/The_Rebel_Alliance_Sourcebook "The Rebel Alliance Sourcebook")*[[149]](#cite_note-TRAS-149)

 [![Mon Mothma and Bail Organa, in an image from The New Essential Chronology](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/3/34/Bail_Organa_and_Mon_Mothma.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20090626184659) [![Mon Mothma and Bail Organa, in an image from The New Essential Chronology](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/3/34/Bail_Organa_and_Mon_Mothma.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/150?cb=20090626184659)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/3/34/Bail_Organa_and_Mon_Mothma.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20090626184659) 

Mon Mothma and Bail Organa, in an image from *The New Essential Chronology*

 

[Mon Mothma](/wiki/Mon_Mothma/Legends "Mon Mothma/Legends") appeared in numerous stories in the Expanded Universe of books, comics, and games, which have since become non-canon and rebranded as [*Star Wars* Legends](/wiki/Star_Wars_Legends "Star Wars Legends").[[150]](#cite_note-Legends_Announcement-150) These stories saw her role in the Rebellion fleshed out, showing her as the leader of the Rebel Alliance. The [1991](/wiki/1991 "1991") novel *[Heir to the Empire](/wiki/Heir_to_the_Empire "Heir to the Empire")*, written by [Timothy Zahn](/wiki/Timothy_Zahn "Timothy Zahn"), showed her becoming [Chief of State](/wiki/Chancellor_(New_Republic) "Chancellor (New Republic)") of the [New Republic](/wiki/New_Republic/Legends "New Republic/Legends"),[[151]](#cite_note-Heir_to_the_Empire-151) setting the stage for her canonical counterpart to become the first chancellor of the New Republic.[[18]](#cite_note-Aftermath-18) The 2005 reference book *[The New Essential Chronology](/wiki/The_New_Essential_Chronology "The New Essential Chronology")* established that the Legends version of Mon Mothma died in her sleep [twenty years](/wiki/24_ABY/Legends "24 ABY/Legends") after the Battle of Endor.[[152]](#cite_note-nec-152) After the character continued appearing in Legends stories, Blakiston became aware of her character's prolific appearances. She was intrigued by this fact[[124]](#cite_note-Blakiston_interview-124)[[125]](#cite_note-Knightley-125) and credited it to what she saw as Mothma's strong personality. Blakiston stated that, despite the character's limited screentime in *Return of the Jedi*, she saw Mothma as an archetypal figure not unlike Darth Vader and Obi-Wan Kenobi.[[125]](#cite_note-Knightley-125)

Furthermore, *[Queen's Shadow](/wiki/Queen%27s_Shadow "Queen's Shadow")* establishes that Mothma was elected senator four [years](/wiki/Standard_year "Standard year") prior to the events of the novel, which is set in [28 BBY](/wiki/28_BBY "28 BBY"). "Nobody's Listening!")" 25. [↑](#cite_ref-MOFSenateJoinDate_25-0) [PenguinRandomHouse-Logo](https://www.penguin.co.uk) [Star Wars: Edge of the Abyss](https://www.penguin.co.uk/books/465299/star-wars-edge-of-the-abyss-by-roanhorse-rebecca/9781804953167) on [Penguin Books'](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Penguin_Random_House "wikipedia:Penguin Random House") [official United Kingdom website](https://www.penguin.co.uk) ([backup link](https://web.archive.org/web/20251212200753/https://www.penguin.co.uk/books/465299/star-wars-edge-of-the-abyss-by-roanhorse-rebecca/9781804953167)) establishes the events of *[Reign of the Empire: The Mask of Fear](/wiki/Reign_of_the_Empire:_The_Mask_of_Fear "Reign of the Empire: The Mask of Fear")* take place thirteen [years](/wiki/Standard_year "Standard year") before the events of *[Reign of the Empire: Edge of the Abyss](/wiki/Reign_of_the_Empire:_Edge_of_the_Abyss "Reign of the Empire: Edge of the Abyss")*. [Instagram-Logo](https://instagram.com) [Rebecca Roanhorse](/wiki/Rebecca_Roanhorse "Rebecca Roanhorse") ([@rebeccaroanhorse](https://instagram.com/rebeccaroanhorse)) on [Instagram](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Instagram "wikipedia:Instagram") ([post](https://instagram.com/p/DMlJiHDs5RJ)): "Title and updated release date of my upcoming STAR WARS novel announced at SDCC. THE EDGE OF THE ABYSS takes place a year before Andor S1." ([backup link](https://archive.ph/8tgEm)) states that *Edge of the Abyss* takes place a year before the events of [*Andor* Season 1](/wiki/Andor_Season_1 "Andor Season 1"), which are set in [5 BBY](/wiki/5_BBY "5 BBY") per the reasoning [here](/wiki/Template:AndorDate "Template:AndorDate"). Therefore, the events of *Edge of the Abyss* must be set in [6 BBY](/wiki/6_BBY "6 BBY"), and the events of *The Mask of Fear* in [19 BBY](/wiki/19_BBY "19 BBY"). During Mon Mothma's interrogation in *Reign of the Empire: The Mask of Fear*, Chapter 45, she says she first joined the Senate thirteen years prior to the events of the novel, which are set in 19 BBY. 26. [↑](#cite_ref-MOFDate_26-0) [PenguinRandomHouse-Logo](https://www.penguin.co.uk) [Star Wars: Edge of the Abyss](https://www.penguin.co.uk/books/465299/star-wars-edge-of-the-abyss-by-roanhorse-rebecca/9781804953167) on [Penguin Books'](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Penguin_Random_House "wikipedia:Penguin Random House") [official United Kingdom website](https://www.penguin.co.uk) ([backup link](https://web.archive.org/web/20251212200753/https://www.penguin.co.uk/books/465299/star-wars-edge-of-the-abyss-by-roanhorse-rebecca/9781804953167)) establishes the events of *[Reign of the Empire: The Mask of Fear](/wiki/Reign_of_the_Empire:_The_Mask_of_Fear "Reign of the Empire: The Mask of Fear")* take place thirteen [years](/wiki/Standard_year "Standard year") before the events of *[Reign of the Empire: Edge of the Abyss](/wiki/Reign_of_the_Empire:_Edge_of_the_Abyss "Reign of the Empire: Edge of the Abyss")*. [Instagram-Logo](https://instagram.com) [Rebecca Roanhorse](/wiki/Rebecca_Roanhorse "Rebecca Roanhorse") ([@rebeccaroanhorse](https://instagram.com/rebeccaroanhorse)) on [Instagram](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Instagram "wikipedia:Instagram") ([post](https://instagram.com/p/DMlJiHDs5RJ)): "Title and updated release date of my upcoming STAR WARS novel announced at SDCC. THE EDGE OF THE ABYSS takes place a year before Andor S1." ([backup link](https://archive.ph/8tgEm)) states that *Edge of the Abyss* takes place a year before the events of [*Andor* Season 1](/wiki/Andor_Season_1 "Andor Season 1"), which are set in [5 BBY](/wiki/5_BBY "5 BBY") per the reasoning [here](/wiki/Template:AndorDate "Template:AndorDate"). Therefore, the events of *Edge of the Abyss* must be set in [6 BBY](/wiki/6_BBY "6 BBY"), and the events of *The Mask of Fear* in [19 BBY](/wiki/19_BBY "19 BBY"). 27. [↑](#cite_ref-QS_Date_27-0) The main story of *[Queen's Shadow](/wiki/Queen%27s_Shadow "Queen's Shadow")* takes place four [years](/wiki/Standard_year "Standard year") after the [Invasion of Naboo](/wiki/Invasion_of_Naboo "Invasion of Naboo"), which *[Star Wars: Galactic Atlas](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Galactic_Atlas "Star Wars: Galactic Atlas")* places in [32 BBY](/wiki/32_BBY "32 BBY"). 28. ↑ [28.0](#cite_ref-HC_40_28-0) [28.1](#cite_ref-HC_40_28-1) [28.2](#cite_ref-HC_40_28-2) [28.3](#cite_ref-HC_40_28-3) [28.4](#cite_ref-HC_40_28-4) [28.5](#cite_ref-HC_40_28-5) [28.6](#cite_ref-HC_40_28-6) [28.7](#cite_ref-HC_40_28-7) [28.8](#cite_ref-HC_40_28-8) [*Star Wars Helmet Collection*: Clone Pilot](/wiki/Star_Wars_Helmet_Collection_40 "Star Wars Helmet Collection 40") Databank A-Z: Moraband–Muftak 29. ↑ [29.0](#cite_ref-Queen's_Hope_29-0) [29.1](#cite_ref-Queen's_Hope_29-1) *[Queen's Hope](/wiki/Queen%27s_Hope "Queen's Hope")* 30. [↑](#cite_ref-MOFDateRebirthAct_51-0) [PenguinRandomHouse-Logo](https://www.penguin.co.uk) [Star Wars: Edge of the Abyss](https://www.penguin.co.uk/books/465299/star-wars-edge-of-the-abyss-by-roanhorse-rebecca/9781804953167) on [Penguin Books'](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Penguin_Random_House "wikipedia:Penguin Random House") [official United Kingdom website](https://www.penguin.co.uk) ([backup link](https://web.archive.org/web/20251212200753/https://www.penguin.co.uk/books/465299/star-wars-edge-of-the-abyss-by-roanhorse-rebecca/9781804953167)) establishes the events of *[Reign of the Empire: The Mask of Fear](/wiki/Reign_of_the_Empire:_The_Mask_of_Fear "Reign of the Empire: The Mask of Fear")* take place thirteen [years](/wiki/Standard_year "Standard year") before the events of *[Reign of the Empire: Edge of the Abyss](/wiki/Reign_of_the_Empire:_Edge_of_the_Abyss "Reign of the Empire: Edge of the Abyss")*. [Instagram-Logo](https://instagram.com) [Rebecca Roanhorse](/wiki/Rebecca_Roanhorse "Rebecca Roanhorse") ([@rebeccaroanhorse](https://instagram.com/rebeccaroanhorse)) on [Instagram](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Instagram "wikipedia:Instagram") ([post](https://instagram.com/p/DMlJiHDs5RJ)): "Title and updated release date of my upcoming STAR WARS novel announced at SDCC. THE EDGE OF THE ABYSS takes place a year before Andor S1." ([backup link](https://archive.ph/8tgEm)) states that *Edge of the Abyss* takes place a year before the events of [*Andor* Season 1](/wiki/Andor_Season_1 "Andor Season 1"), which are set in [5 BBY](/wiki/5_BBY "5 BBY") per the reasoning [here](/wiki/Template:AndorDate "Template:AndorDate"). Therefore, the events of *Edge of the Abyss* must be set in [6 BBY](/wiki/6_BBY "6 BBY"), and the events of *The Mask of Fear* in [19 BBY](/wiki/19_BBY "19 BBY"). 52. [↑](#cite_ref-Jalindi_Date_76-0) The trivia guide for *[Star Wars Rebels: Heroes of Mandalore](/wiki/Star_Wars_Rebels:_Heroes_of_Mandalore "Star Wars Rebels: Heroes of Mandalore")* states that [Bo-Katan Kryze](/wiki/Bo-Katan_Kryze "Bo-Katan Kryze") was redesigned to advance the character's age by "18 [years](/wiki/Standard_year "Standard year") or so". As she was last seen was in *[The Lawless](/wiki/The_Lawless "The Lawless")*, which was dated to [19 BBY](/wiki/19_BBY "19 BBY") by *[Star Wars: Galactic Atlas](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Galactic_Atlas "Star Wars: Galactic Atlas")*, it can be assumed that the events of *Heroes of Mandalore* take place in approximately [1 BBY](/wiki/1_BBY "1 BBY"). As [In the Name of the Rebellion](/wiki/In_the_Name_of_the_Rebellion "In the Name of the Rebellion") takes place shortly after *Heroes of Mandalore*, it can be assumed it is also around the [year](/wiki/Standard_year "Standard year") 1 [BBY](/wiki/%27ABY-BBY%27_dating_system "'ABY-BBY' dating system"). 77. [↑](#cite_ref-SotE_Date_82-0) **Mon Mothma** became actively involved in what became the [Alliance to Restore the Republic](/wiki/Alliance_to_Restore_the_Republic "Alliance to Restore the Republic") after the [skirmish in the Archeon Nebula](/wiki/Operation_Handoff "Operation Handoff") in [2 BBY](/wiki/2_BBY "2 BBY"), which took place in the *[Star Wars Rebels](/wiki/Star_Wars_Rebels "Star Wars Rebels")* episode "[Secret Cargo](/wiki/Secret_Cargo "Secret Cargo")," placing the events of *[Star Wars: Secrets of the Empire](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Secrets_of_the_Empire "Star Wars: Secrets of the Empire")* after those events. The inclusion of [K-2SO](/wiki/K-2SO "K-2SO") means that this event takes place prior to the [Battle of Scarif](/wiki/Battle_of_Scarif "Battle of Scarif") in [1 BBY](/wiki/1_BBY "1 BBY"), in which the [droid](/wiki/Droid "Droid") was [killed](/wiki/Death "Death"). 83. [↑](#cite_ref-Part_Seven_112-0) [AhsokaTitle-Template](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Ahsoka "Star Wars: Ahsoka") *[Star Wars: Ahsoka](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Ahsoka "Star Wars: Ahsoka")* — "[Part Seven: Dreams and Madness](/wiki/Part_Seven:_Dreams_and_Madness "Part Seven: Dreams and Madness")" 113. [↑](#cite_ref-Date_113-0) [SWInsider](/wiki/Star_Wars_Insider "Star Wars Insider") "[A Certain Point of View](/wiki/A_Certain_Point_of_View_(department) "A Certain Point of View (department)")" — [*Star Wars Insider* 228](/wiki/Star_Wars_Insider_228 "Star Wars Insider 228") dates the events of "[Part Seven: Dreams and Madness](/wiki/Part_Seven:_Dreams_and_Madness "Part Seven: Dreams and Madness")" to nine [years](/wiki/Standard_year "Standard year") after [*Star Wars*: Episode IV *A New Hope*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_IV_A_New_Hope "Star Wars: Episode IV A New Hope"), which corresponds to [9 ABY](/wiki/9_ABY "9 ABY") per *[Star Wars: Timelines](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Timelines "Star Wars: Timelines")*. Preceding episodes, also take place in that year, since they take place after *[Star Wars: The Book of Boba Fett](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Book_of_Boba_Fett "Star Wars: The Book of Boba Fett")*, which is dated to 9 [ABY](/wiki/%27ABY-BBY%27_dating_system "'ABY-BBY' dating system") according to *Timelines*. As "[Part Eight: The Jedi, the Witch, and the Warlord](/wiki/Part_Eight:_The_Jedi,_the_Witch,_and_the_Warlord "Part Eight: The Jedi, the Witch, and the Warlord")" takes place shortly after Part Seven, the events of [*Ahsoka*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Ahsoka "Star Wars: Ahsoka") as a whole must all take place within the same year. 114.
